  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_caf4ca2d-cb25-462d-a204-5ab1f50b0650'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div id="review_9202028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9202028" />
    <a title="Amy Galaviz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/528777-amy-galaviz"><img alt="Amy Galaviz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1298567499p2/528777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9202028?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Galaviz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Galaviz" href="/user/show/528777-amy-galaviz">Amy Galaviz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9202028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9511583307427232979">I've never been interested in reading or read a book of the fantasy genre before, but I was pleasantly surprised. All characters were fleshed out extremely well; for example, I nearly cried when Raistlin and Caramon lost both their parents, I could understand Raistlin's jealously at Caramon stealing his dream girl. Raistlin's competitiveness with Caramon is the classic nerdy brother vs. attractive/jock brother conflict. Eccentric characters such as Flint the dwarf and Tas the kender made me laug</span>
  <span id="freeText9511583307427232979" style="display:none">I've never been interested in reading or read a book of the fantasy genre before, but I was pleasantly surprised. All characters were fleshed out extremely well; for example, I nearly cried when Raistlin and Caramon lost both their parents, I could understand Raistlin's jealously at Caramon stealing his dream girl. Raistlin's competitiveness with Caramon is the classic nerdy brother vs. attractive/jock brother conflict. Eccentric characters such as Flint the dwarf and Tas the kender made me laugh out loud. Beneath the surface of tracing Raistlin's path from a precocious young child to a wizard, the book illustrates the hardships of adolescence that all of us go through. Also, the larger societal conflicts in the book (humans vs. elves, hill dwarves vs. mountain dwarves, kender as outcasts, violence &amp; propoganda enacted by followers of Belzor) are allegories of social, racial, and religious warfare seen throughout history. A very moving book and I would be glad to read the others in the series if they promise to be just as good or better. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9511583307427232979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1392206648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1392206648" />
    <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo"><img alt="Alfred Haplo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599680519p2/34550725.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1392206648?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alfred Haplo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alfred Haplo" href="/user/show/34550725-alfred-haplo">Alfred Haplo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=sf-fantasy-mytho">sf-fantasy-mytho</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34550725-alfred-haplo?shelf=1970-to-1999">1970-to-1999</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1392206648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17614792259861136860">As far as fantasy goes, I became a real fan with Dragonlance, specifically those authored by Margaret Weis and Tracy Hickman. Those books are forever and ever and evermore - this is my inner teenage speak! - the benchmark for all my fantasy reading. Which is not saying very much, or setting very high expectations when the minimum standard is pulp. I am certainly a slightly more discerning reader now, having read better works, but when it comes to feelings of nostalgia, no other fantasy series * </span>
  <span id="freeText17614792259861136860" style="display:none">As far as fantasy goes, I became a real fan with Dragonlance, specifically those authored by Margaret Weis and Tracy Hickman. Those books are forever and ever and evermore - this is my inner teenage speak! - the benchmark for all my fantasy reading. Which is not saying very much, or setting very high expectations when the minimum standard is pulp. I am certainly a slightly more discerning reader now, having read better works, but when it comes to feelings of nostalgia, no other fantasy series * have a better claim on mine. <br /><br />More succinctly, <i>Raistlin Chronicles #1 - The Soulforge</i> is recommended for fans. For everyone else, this is probably a 2-star rating for mediocre writing, too much tell, and very little sentimental significance. Those who have enjoyed <i>Chronicles</i>* and <i>Legends</i>* will appreciate the beginnings of young Raistlin Majere in <i>The Soulforge</i>, and the precursors for his life’s dark path. Fundamental to the salvation of Raistlin’s soul is his lifelong friendships and how they come to be forged. The Companions, all of whom are featured here with the Majere twins - squabbles, comedy, adventures and all - to the pleasure of my memory. <br /><br />Honestly, I was a tad disappointed to glean very little new information that was not already choice morsels in other Dragonlance books. Sure, there are biographical tidbits to be had like Raistlin's aversion to a certain herb and his adolescent crush but his internal development is static. Raistlin just becomes a more concentrated version of himself later. Already familiar to fans are his bouts of self-doubts and ambition, bitterness and cunning but by and large, older Raistlin in the future is rather like young Raistlin in the past… ooh, maybe? Never mind. The story is just not that clever, but there is a twisty bit at the end that was unexpected. <br /><br />I had fun, and fun can forgive much. On to <i>Raistlin Chronicles #2 - Brothers in Arms.</i><br /><br /><br />[* <b>Dragonlance: Chronicles</b>: Dragons of Autumn Twilight #1, Dragons of Winter Night #2, Dragons of Spring Dawning #3 &amp; <b>Dragonlance: Legends</b>: Time of the Twins #1, War of the Twins #2, Test of the Twins #3.]</span>
  <a data-text-id="17614792259861136860" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15685077737365839526">This book doesn't quite reach the heights of the <i>Legends</i> trilogy but definitely shows a more mature sense of character and plotting than the seminal, though flawed, <i>Chronicles</i> that started us off on our journeys through the world of Krynn.<br/><br/>Want to really know how sickly, sneaky Raistlin became the golden-skinned freakazoid we meet during the Wars of the Lance? Well, this is the book for you:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596639896i/29920137.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As much as I enjoyed all the Raistlin stuff, my enjoyment from the re-read came more from getting to know, </span>
  <span id="freeText15685077737365839526" style="display:none">This book doesn't quite reach the heights of the <i>Legends</i> trilogy but definitely shows a more mature sense of character and plotting than the seminal, though flawed, <i>Chronicles</i> that started us off on our journeys through the world of Krynn.<br><br>Want to really know how sickly, sneaky Raistlin became the golden-skinned freakazoid we meet during the Wars of the Lance? Well, this is the book for you:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596639896i/29920137.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As much as I enjoyed all the Raistlin stuff, my enjoyment from the re-read came more from getting to know, even indirectly, the younger incarnations of familiar characters like his twin brother Caramon, mercurial older half-sister Kitiara, their friend Sturm, and so on.<br><br>On the whole I felt this book was perhaps 50 pages too long, maybe some of the dreary details of the young Raistlin's schooling at Krynn's shittiest version of Hogwarts could have been skipped, but I'm glad to have revisited it and am now keen to read the sequel about the brothers Majeres' early adventures, whose existence I only just learned about, for the first time.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596640364i/29920271._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br></span>

<div id="review_3410084981" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3410084981" />
    <a title="C.T. Phipps" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5873287-c-t-phipps"><img alt="C.T. Phipps" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401836765p2/5873287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3410084981?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.T. Phipps" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.T. Phipps" href="/user/show/5873287-c-t-phipps">C.T. Phipps</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5873287-c-t-phipps?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3410084981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9380635503809896990">Raistlin Majere remains one of my favorite characters in fiction, though I've since come to also associate him with many qualities I loathed about my teenage self. You know, the entitled know-it-all who probably had a lot more issues with women than I would have if I just treated them as people. <br/><br/>THE SOULFORGE is one of the best of the Dragonlance novels other than the original six and details the origins of the one of Nineties' fantasies best antiheroes. Magic was always the great love of Raistl</span>
  <span id="freeText9380635503809896990" style="display:none">Raistlin Majere remains one of my favorite characters in fiction, though I've since come to also associate him with many qualities I loathed about my teenage self. You know, the entitled know-it-all who probably had a lot more issues with women than I would have if I just treated them as people. <br /><br />THE SOULFORGE is one of the best of the Dragonlance novels other than the original six and details the origins of the one of Nineties' fantasies best antiheroes. Magic was always the great love of Raistlin, even when he was too young for such things, because it is the one he could always control completely. <br /><br />My only regret about this book is we're still some years away from Raistlin's darkest actions and thus when he's at his most interesting. Oh and that I kind of prefer Kitiara Uth Matar to Raistlin. I would have loved to have read Margaret Weis' take on her rise to power. That's just me as a fan nitpicking, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9380635503809896990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7278134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7278134" />
    <a title="Victor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/371305-victor"><img alt="Victor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1191543289p2/371305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7278134?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victor" href="/user/show/371305-victor">Victor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780786906451" href="/book/show/534456.The_Soulforge">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7278134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4883379637274013615">Here is a good example of what would have happened if Harry Potter turned evil. This is a great book to read if you are sick of mamby pamsy wizards and want to read a good book about a sickly kid who turns into someone who is “not a very nice person” (as said by one of the Hobbit-like characters in a different book from this series). The only flaw is that while it is quite informative about the character of Raistlin Majere (the golden guy on the cover), we do not get to see him use much magic. I</span>
  <span id="freeText4883379637274013615" style="display:none">Here is a good example of what would have happened if Harry Potter turned evil. This is a great book to read if you are sick of mamby pamsy wizards and want to read a good book about a sickly kid who turns into someone who is “not a very nice person” (as said by one of the Hobbit-like characters in a different book from this series). The only flaw is that while it is quite informative about the character of Raistlin Majere (the golden guy on the cover), we do not get to see him use much magic. I personally would have liked to have seen him go crazy at some point like Willow from Buffy the Vampire Slayer, but instead, seeing that he is only a novice in this book, though a very adept one, we get to see him use his mind and skills at casting illusions. All the same, this is a very well written book where you really get to know a lot of the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4883379637274013615" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1306948814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1306948814" />
    <a title="Alan Hernandez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30259487-alan-hernandez"><img alt="Alan Hernandez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485102843p2/30259487.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1306948814?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alan Hernandez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alan Hernandez" href="/user/show/30259487-alan-hernandez">Alan Hernandez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1306948814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8398256812294858593">Having not read any dragonlance books prior to reading this one, I approached this with the unique perspective of having no pre-formed bias for the characters. For those that don't know, this book serves as an origin story for some of the main characters in the dragonlance books, specifically for the physically weak but intellectual Raistlin. <br/><br/>Overall I found the book to be an enjoyable read. The main cast are an entertaining bunch, each personality greatly contrasting the others. Though co-autho</span>
  <span id="freeText8398256812294858593" style="display:none">Having not read any dragonlance books prior to reading this one, I approached this with the unique perspective of having no pre-formed bias for the characters. For those that don't know, this book serves as an origin story for some of the main characters in the dragonlance books, specifically for the physically weak but intellectual Raistlin. <br /><br />Overall I found the book to be an enjoyable read. The main cast are an entertaining bunch, each personality greatly contrasting the others. Though co-authored, the story maintains a consistent voice. The reader gets a small taste of the vast world that is Krynn through references to distant lands with several races. Each race comes with its own stereotypes and rivalries with other races. Weis does a great job in establishing the interpersonal relationships between the characters and the characters remain consistent in their personalities. <br /><br />Every so often there is an unexpected twist: a scenario that Raistlin is thrust into where the reader is allowed a glimpse into the true nature of the young mage. Raistlin's inner journey into wizarding manhood is evident in his constant search for more knowledge and power. Though quite talented, the hardships of his life is not lost. He is generally frail and sickly. He is also cold and untrusting. His twin brother Caramon serves as a mirror of that which Raistlin wishes to be/have and therefore further increases his lust for power. Though I am unfamiliar with the general dragonlance tale, I thoroughly enjoyed its origin story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8398256812294858593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2576733-jeff-yoak?shelf=audio-collection">audio-collection</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920484102" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer382651896917620401">The Dragonlance series was the second set of fiction that I read on my own for enjoyment as a child. I fell utterly in love with them, and read them many times. Discovering that they're now available in audio, I decided to revisit them. I discovered that many more books were written in the world after I outgrew my interest, and decided to read them in the order of the story's chronology.<br/><br/>It was an interesting experience starting with The Soulforge. Though it was new to me, it was very nostalgic. </span>
  <span id="freeText382651896917620401" style="display:none">The Dragonlance series was the second set of fiction that I read on my own for enjoyment as a child. I fell utterly in love with them, and read them many times. Discovering that they're now available in audio, I decided to revisit them. I discovered that many more books were written in the world after I outgrew my interest, and decided to read them in the order of the story's chronology.<br /><br />It was an interesting experience starting with The Soulforge. Though it was new to me, it was very nostalgic. Not only are all of the characters extremely well-known to me, but most of the events of this novel are referred to "later" and the experience is one of filling in the details of something you already "know."<br /><br />I enjoyed this visit to Krynn. I'm looking forward to staying a while.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9800122507988815227">This is the story of Raistlin as a child and how he found magic. It is also the story of how the Heroes of the Lance came to be and their first adventure. This book had it all and it is a must read if you are into Dragonlance. It made me laugh( how could you not with any scene involving Tas). I was sad at one scene and it also provided me with a detailed account how Raistlin came to be in the original series. Raistlin is a one the most interesting characters and this book helped me understand hi</span>
  <span id="freeText9800122507988815227" style="display:none">This is the story of Raistlin as a child and how he found magic. It is also the story of how the Heroes of the Lance came to be and their first adventure. This book had it all and it is a must read if you are into Dragonlance. It made me laugh( how could you not with any scene involving Tas). I was sad at one scene and it also provided me with a detailed account how Raistlin came to be in the original series. Raistlin is a one the most interesting characters and this book helped me understand him more. I highly recommend this book even if you are not into fantasy. I believe everyone would enjoy this.</span>

<div id="review_545277353" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/545277353" />
    <a title="Joshua Mandell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13753567-joshua-mandell"><img alt="Joshua Mandell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455290005p2/13753567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/545277353?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joshua Mandell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joshua Mandell" href="/user/show/13753567-joshua-mandell">Joshua Mandell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer545277353" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13519936841660292928">I'm something of a fan of the Dragonlance mythos in general; the Chronicles intrigued me and seemed quite well done, and now from one of the authors of those books comes this first in a new series, the Raistlin Chronicles. When I saw that there was indeed going to be a "Raistlin Chronicles" I was highly interested. After all, Raistlin is in my opinion and in the opinions of many other Dragonlance readers the most well thought out of the protagonist characters, the most complicated in terms of pe</span>
  <span id="freeText13519936841660292928" style="display:none">I'm something of a fan of the Dragonlance mythos in general; the Chronicles intrigued me and seemed quite well done, and now from one of the authors of those books comes this first in a new series, the Raistlin Chronicles. When I saw that there was indeed going to be a "Raistlin Chronicles" I was highly interested. After all, Raistlin is in my opinion and in the opinions of many other Dragonlance readers the most well thought out of the protagonist characters, the most complicated in terms of personality, and one of the most important characters throughout. The Time of the Twins, War of the Twins, and Test of the Twins focused further on Raistlin and Caramon -- and I'm glad to say that this series, likewise, isn't focusing purely on Raistlin, but it's also focusing on the relationship between him and his brother. Although he often acts caustically toward him, being quick to scold, there is some real affection there and that comes out in this book.<br /><br />The Soulforge tells the story of Raistlin's early life, his apprenticeship in the school of Master Theobald (A hilariously inept mage himself, at least as this book portrays him, but certainly capable enough to help some small children take their first steps on the path of magical learning), and then his Test of High Sorcery. The writing is suspenseful and kept me reading, and it was the first book I've read in some time that has kept me this interested throughout. I'm not going to spoil any more of the plot than I already have; I recommend this to anyone who likes fantasy and I'm going to try to find the second and third books in the series when I get the opportunity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13519936841660292928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1909299679" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1909299679" />
    <a title="Justin VanShaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/64842238-justin-vanshaar"><img alt="Justin VanShaar" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1909299679?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Justin VanShaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Justin VanShaar" href="/user/show/64842238-justin-vanshaar">Justin VanShaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1909299679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8124307368496028645">The Soulforge is the story of Raistlin Majere's childhood years, a more in-depth account of his fathers and mother's depression and death than was told in Dragons of Winter Night. His bullying is emphasized more than the small record we were given in Test of the Twins. This story tells of his introduction to the mage-school where his "soul is forged in the crucible of magic."<br/><br/>In my opinion, this is one of the best Dragonlance books ever written! It excellently answered some of my questions about </span>
  <span id="freeText8124307368496028645" style="display:none">The Soulforge is the story of Raistlin Majere's childhood years, a more in-depth account of his fathers and mother's depression and death than was told in Dragons of Winter Night. His bullying is emphasized more than the small record we were given in Test of the Twins. This story tells of his introduction to the mage-school where his "soul is forged in the crucible of magic."<br /><br />In my opinion, this is one of the best Dragonlance books ever written! It excellently answered some of my questions about Raistlin, although I wish the authors had allowed him to use more magic instead of only sleight-of-hand and mental strength. The idea that his twin, Caramon, took Miranda, a girl Raist was infatuated with, is an interesting explanation for Raist's resentment of his brother and romantic relationships in general. I still wonder if that's the way it really happened, since "the name of Raistlin Majere had become legend over the years. A great deal that has been written, told, and sung about the great mage is either false or a distortion of the truth. I am guilty of some of this myself..."<br /><br />His jealousy of his good-looking, stronger twin; fighting love as smothering as it is nurturing, and wanting to become a greater person is a natural feeling to which every person who has grown up with a sibling could relate. Overall, Weis' prose is compelling and effective. I easily recommend it to my friends.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8124307368496028645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7853397843239654484" style="display:none">Raistlin Majere, greatest wizard of all time! Becoming interested in Raistlin when I first heard the song “The Soulforged” by the group Blind Guardian, many years passed before I read the first Dragonlance book, Dragons ofAutumn Twilight. That novel further grew my interest in Raistlin, as wizards have always been my favoured class in video games and D&amp;D. Finally reading this book, more than 10 years after discovering who this man was, was the greatest treat I have given myself, in a literary sense. I have read upon many wizards, but none have I loved more than this one. Certainly, he is a cruel man, easy to hate, however, as is suggested by him attain his own novel, he is also one to love. I look forward to reading more in the Dragonlance series, thus seeing where his later years take him, as I have only read this and Dragons of Autumn Twilight.<br />Anyone that is interested in a fantasy story that gives magic without overusing it, this is truly the story for you. You will find yourself in awe as you struggle between loving and hating Raistlin Majere at the same time.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8348899667903859578">The Twins Caramon and Raistlin are opposites, Caramon got the body, Raistlin got the brain. As children in Solace their older half sister Kitiara took care of the boys. She knew Caramon would grow up fine, he had a strong body that would have no trouble working a field or swinging a sword. Raistlin on the other hand she feared for, he was lean and sickly and needed more attention than his brother. Kitiara arranged for a passing Archmage to meet Raistlin and sponsor him in the local wizard school</span>
  <span id="freeText8348899667903859578" style="display:none">The Twins Caramon and Raistlin are opposites, Caramon got the body, Raistlin got the brain. As children in Solace their older half sister Kitiara took care of the boys. She knew Caramon would grow up fine, he had a strong body that would have no trouble working a field or swinging a sword. Raistlin on the other hand she feared for, he was lean and sickly and needed more attention than his brother. Kitiara arranged for a passing Archmage to meet Raistlin and sponsor him in the local wizard school. Raistlin goes to school while Caramon works a near by farm. It is during this time we see why Raistlin is so mean to Caramon at times. Raistlin meets a girl whom he would have given up magic for, that is until he spied on her "engaged" with his brother. From that point on Raistlin swears the pursuit of power and magic would be his only love. The book ends with Raistlin taking his test at the Tower of High Sorcery, earning his red robes, his gold skin and his hourglass eyes. Love this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8348899667903859578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer5554302347942418358">After reading some of my short stories, a friend gushed about how similar it was to Soulforge and insisted I pick it up. Though I don't personally see the connection, this story was still my enjoyable entry into the Dragonlance setting.<br/><br/>I dislike prequels in general, so having read this first before Chronicles was a great choice. The characters seem to come alive a bit more so than Dragons of Autumn Twilight, and it's nicely put together origin story for one of the settings more enigmatic and pop</span>
  <span id="freeText5554302347942418358" style="display:none">After reading some of my short stories, a friend gushed about how similar it was to Soulforge and insisted I pick it up. Though I don't personally see the connection, this story was still my enjoyable entry into the Dragonlance setting.<br /><br />I dislike prequels in general, so having read this first before Chronicles was a great choice. The characters seem to come alive a bit more so than Dragons of Autumn Twilight, and it's nicely put together origin story for one of the settings more enigmatic and popular characters. The formation of Raistlin's personality as he grows up feels natural, and doesn't read as though it was shoe-horned in as an excuse to explain how he acts later in the timeline.<br /><br />I would definitely recommend this to anyone looking to grab the core Dragonlance books. Start with this book before going to the Chronicles trilogy. If you're a fan of these style of high fantasy novels, you won't be disappointed.</span>

<div id="review_1025129545" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1025129545" />
    <a title="Tifa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14462526-tifa"><img alt="Tifa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1364091594p2/14462526.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1025129545?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tifa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tifa" href="/user/show/14462526-tifa">Tifa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1025129545" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer493447585676821008">I didn't realize what a huge influence the Dragonlance books had on me as a teenager developing as a reader and writer until recently. When I started to re-read the original two trilogies, I was really excited to find the writing was as good as, or even better, than I remembered. Then I read a few of the "in-between" novels and was disappointed by the way the writing had changed over the years. Fortunately, this book was really back up to Weis' usual standards. The writing was done well and inte</span>
  <span id="freeText493447585676821008" style="display:none">I didn't realize what a huge influence the Dragonlance books had on me as a teenager developing as a reader and writer until recently. When I started to re-read the original two trilogies, I was really excited to find the writing was as good as, or even better, than I remembered. Then I read a few of the "in-between" novels and was disappointed by the way the writing had changed over the years. Fortunately, this book was really back up to Weis' usual standards. The writing was done well and interesting, the character development was solid, and the story filled in a lot of the blanks that we readers had wondered about over the years. Overall, I really enjoyed this book more than I thought I would, based on the later Dragonlance books. If you are a Raistlin or twins' fan, this is a must-read.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13409751175293069237" style="display:none">This is one of the best books I've read in a long time. <br /><br />I haven't read too much of Dragonlance - Only the Chronicles and Legends so far - but Raistlin and Caramon are my absolute favorite characters in the series and some of my favorite literary characters of all time. As you could probably guess, this is my favorite Dragonlance book so far. <br /><br />This one had a big "magic school" theme which made it a bit like Harry Potter, but also showed how the companions all met. I liked seeing that. <br /><br />I've always found Raistlin a relateable character - smart but not physically strong, ambitious, and not really good or evil. <br /><br />Overall this book was incredibly enjoyable.<br /><br /><br />Also: This book needs a better cover. Raistlin looks like some sort of girly male model in a fantasy setting...</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10471285379524637799">I really liked this book. It was a fairly easy read, but it was enjoyable. The characters were colorful, and you could watch them change over time. There were characters I hated at first, but grew to love, and characters I didn't mind at first, but grew to hate. I liked the way it was split up into smaller books, allowing for different stories to be told through the progression of time. Everything ended up being relevant, so it worked well when it all came together. I own a few other books from </span>
  <span id="freeText10471285379524637799" style="display:none">I really liked this book. It was a fairly easy read, but it was enjoyable. The characters were colorful, and you could watch them change over time. There were characters I hated at first, but grew to love, and characters I didn't mind at first, but grew to hate. I liked the way it was split up into smaller books, allowing for different stories to be told through the progression of time. Everything ended up being relevant, so it worked well when it all came together. I own a few other books from the Dragonlance series, but I'd never read them. This book has definitely helped encourage me to pick up some of the others. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/468051255" />
    <a title="Tero Luikku" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13709933-tero-luikku"><img alt="Tero Luikku" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550745762p2/13709933.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468051255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3922181791387392885">Soulforge was the first Dragonlance-book I didn't feel like it's suppose to be the backbone of a tabletop RPG-adventure. Even though it's constructed pretty much in a similar fashion to the other, building up to a huge boss-battle in the end, the flow and scope makes it more personal, makes it feel more like a diary confessions of a single person.<br/><br/>That's what makes the Soulforge quite unique in Dragonlance-books, and that's what draws me to this book even more so than the fact that it's Raistlin.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('m1xP1nrYmNUNKvtBU/lsDNfcSNxfxpbxbLiZFK/jmVUE28abPjCDBATLzpI6i21PZQg3kidAa1BreHqtUHO5Iw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gHfubeJW43eQBmh59Maqk+oUksyAqrgnzU0AE0j/GOMf8Gcgpr74ppnnXaqdtKvQWMDtgvgsRYbKjeOqt284lQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer10475311926682743197">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two para</span>
  <span id="freeText10475311926682743197" style="display:none">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two paranormal romance novels, Fallen Angel and Warrior Angel, with my daughter, Elizabeth Baldwin. I graduated from the University of Missouri–Columbia and now live in Wisconsin with dogs, Max, Dixie, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am currently working on the third book in the Dragon Brigade series, the Seventh Sigil. The first book is Shadow Raiders. The second book is Storm Riders, coming out from Tor in July 2013. <br /><br />My hobby is flyball racing with my dogs, Dixie, a border collie, and two crackhead Shelties, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am the owner of the company, Margaret Weis Productions, publisher of RPGs. Our newest project is creating the RPG for the wonderful TV series, Firefly. Shiny!</span>
